  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_25cb84c2-007b-42a8-818b-77e03e6c732f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer5024985395852274043">In a kingdom of merciless tyrants, Jebel Rum's family is honored as royalty because his father is the executioner. But Rashed Rum is near retirement. And when he goes, there will be a contest to determine his successor. It is a contest that thin, puny Jebel has no chance of winning. Humiliated and ashamed, Jebel sets out on a quest to the faraway home of a legendary fire g</span>
  <span id="freeText5024985395852274043" style="display:none">In a kingdom of merciless tyrants, Jebel Rum's family is honored as royalty because his father is the executioner. But Rashed Rum is near retirement. And when he goes, there will be a contest to determine his successor. It is a contest that thin, puny Jebel has no chance of winning. Humiliated and ashamed, Jebel sets out on a quest to the faraway home of a legendary fire god to beg for inhuman powers so that he can become the most lethal of men. He must take with him a slave, named Tel Hesani, to be sacrificed to the god. It will be a dark and brutal journey filled with lynch mobs, suicide cults, terrible monsters, and worse, monstrous men. But to Jebel, the risk is worth it. To retrieve his honor . . . To wield unimaginable power . . . To become . . . The thin executioner<br />Inspired by the<i></i><i>Adventures of Huckleberry Finn</i>, international bestselling master of horror Darren Shan takes readers on a thrilling, fast-paced journey into a nightmarish world where compassion and kindness are the greatest crimes of all.</span>

<div id="review_381774274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381774274" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11473232-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545983518p2/11473232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381774274?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/11473232-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381774274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11316964940814467125">This book was absolutely thrilling! Many people that have also read this book are saying things like it didn't live up to the standards of Shan's other books, or that there weren't any twists in the plot, but that's what made this book even better! People are missing the meaning of this book! Yes, it was a fantasy. A nice one at that, there were plenty of gorey details; executions, whippings, slaves, etc. But the best part of the book was that this spoiled brat, Jebel Rum, became a hero. Not som</span>
  <span id="freeText11316964940814467125" style="display:none">This book was absolutely thrilling! Many people that have also read this book are saying things like it didn't live up to the standards of Shan's other books, or that there weren't any twists in the plot, but that's what made this book even better! People are missing the meaning of this book! Yes, it was a fantasy. A nice one at that, there were plenty of gorey details; executions, whippings, slaves, etc. But the best part of the book was that this spoiled brat, Jebel Rum, became a hero. Not someone who was well-liked or that was popular or was out to be heroic, but someone who stood up for what he believed in and thought of all people, from kings to slaves, as equals. There was also one part of this book that really touched me and got my mind thinking. The scene where Jebel's on a river in his near dath experience with the death god from his religion, and he looks around and asks who all the other people in boats on the river are. And the god replies saying something about how each person is seeing what they expected to see. For instance, Jebel saw the god of his religion because that's what he expected to see. Someone else who believed in a different deity or entity would see whatever god that was. So, this gives you a sense of the fact that no one religion is greater than another. Each religion or set of beliefs is unique and has every right to be in existence. Nothing is "right" or "wrong". I mean, we're all human so what do we know about the afterlife anyway? Overall, Jebel's courage gets him through this epic journey as well as his will to never give up. In the end he is humbled by all of the experiences that he had been through. I would highly recommend this book to anyone looking for a good action filled read with some meaning, especially guys. I just loaned this book to my boyfriend to read and he absolutely LOVES it so far! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11316964940814467125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I was expecting to find a really engaging book from Darren Shan and was not disappointed at all! The imagination of lots of cultures, the adventures the protagonists experience, the character development of the main boy... The ideas and throughts they exchanged about life, death, religion, society... I loved every aspect of this book and I gladly recommend this to everyone! </span>

<div id="review_2351665463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351665463" />
    <a title="Marshall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80248806-marshall"><img alt="Marshall" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2351665463?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marshall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marshall" href="/user/show/80248806-marshall">Marshall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351665463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11416900262066686164">The Thin Executioner<br/>	The book im reviewing is <i>The Thin Executioner</i> by Darren Shan. Shan has talked in many interviews talking about how “writing <i>The Thin Executioner</i> has been one of his favorites so far..”. Normally Shan sticks to making sequels to his novels, but <i>The Thin Executioner</i> is one that stands alone with how much time he's put into it. Much like his other books but different in its own amazing way <i>The Thin Executioners</i> context is that of a young scrawny kid with an unlikely mentor can </span>
  <span id="freeText11416900262066686164" style="display:none">The Thin Executioner<br />	The book im reviewing is <i>The Thin Executioner</i> by Darren Shan. Shan has talked in many interviews talking about how “writing <i>The Thin Executioner</i> has been one of his favorites so far..”. Normally Shan sticks to making sequels to his novels, but <i>The Thin Executioner</i> is one that stands alone with how much time he's put into it. Much like his other books but different in its own amazing way <i>The Thin Executioners</i> context is that of a young scrawny kid with an unlikely mentor can become a true hero and be loved but hated in there own way. The book’s theme aligned with his others being thriller with a perfect mix of horror. My opinion of the book is that it was amazing in every way.<br />	Careful, because here comes some spoilers. A young Jebel Rum is dishonored by his high ranking father who is an executioner who lives in a place with slavery. So Jebel asks the king to go on a quest to speak to a god to give him strength but he must sacrifice a slave. So he meets Tel Hasani offering him the freedom of his wife and kids. So Jebel and Tel venture off, and at first their trip is easy. they also meet some wealthy friends Master Bush and Blair that end up turning on them. Jebel and Tel make it through many hard times and Jebel towards the end when they meet a cult and are put through torture start to become friends. At the end of there Quest Jebel tricks Master Bush and Baire to there death and Tel and Jebel make it to the gods home in the mountain. But the leader of the cult finds them and wounds Tel Hasani as he wants him the owner of the cult to have the power but he is struck down. When Jebel refuses to kill his friend, the god sees him as a good person and grants him his wish. While Tel Hassani is dead and Jebel mourns his friend, he makes it home in time to become the executioner, but Jebel has a change of heart and enforces new laws like jail and better judgment. My favorite part can honestly not be determined but the whole book showing how close Jebel and Tel Hassani become.<br />	In the beginning of the book I began to feel for Jebel and how he was dishonored by his father, but by the time he begins his quest you see how badly he treats Tel Hasani and feel like hating the protagonist. And the respect you have for Tel Hasani due to the fact that he puts up with Jebel in order to save his family. And towards the middle of there journey you learn to hate Master Bush and Blair but due to the hatred for them Tel Hasani and Jebel become closer and Jebel finally begins to see his “slave” as a friend he can rely on because out in there world they can't trust anyone else. Jebels decision to embark on the quest is like any other he wants the respect of his father and the respect of everyone around him, and also he wants to be strong enough to support the love of his dream girl. And while I loved the whole book the ending was the greatest when Jebel learns to despise murder and finally becomes a good person after he makes it home in time in order to become the new executioner. While we feel the loss of Tell Hasani, we now know that he wasn't sacrificed and Jebel grew close to him. And after it tells of how Jebel was able to bring on new laws like jail and better judgment instead of murdering as an executioner. And it tells of his family as he's older and how he went for a woman who actually loved him and named his first son after Tel Hasani which made me happier than ever for Jebel.<br />	I loved everything about the book much like Shann’s other books I couldn't put this one down no matter how hard I tried and always found myself being sucked into it. Anyone into thrillers or anything interesting I would highly recommend this book Shan has been my favorite writer for as long as i can remember and any one of his books I would recommend in a heartbeat. There's only one thing don't read this book unless you want to find yourself thinking about what could be happening next anytime your reading the book or not along with being sucked into Jebel Rums world and feelings.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11416900262066686164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216628263" />
    <a title="Lydia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5994898-lydia"><img alt="Lydia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392890595p2/5994898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216628263?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia" href="/user/show/5994898-lydia">Lydia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216628263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2407826815404990821">This was a very creative, original, enjoyable book in every way. I was fascinated by the Jordan-inspired names. It was very interesting to see darker-skinned and -haired people as the beautiful upper-class, and lighter-skinned, fairer-haired people as the slaves. The religious take was very thought-inspiring as well. I only remembered about halfway through that the book was inspired by Huckleberry Finn, and that remembrance brought even more meaning to an already wonderful story. It's about bein</span>
  <span id="freeText2407826815404990821" style="display:none">This was a very creative, original, enjoyable book in every way. I was fascinated by the Jordan-inspired names. It was very interesting to see darker-skinned and -haired people as the beautiful upper-class, and lighter-skinned, fairer-haired people as the slaves. The religious take was very thought-inspiring as well. I only remembered about halfway through that the book was inspired by Huckleberry Finn, and that remembrance brought even more meaning to an already wonderful story. It's about being open-minded to ideas other than those you were raised with, learning to value life, and learning to love someone for what's on the inside rather than outward beauty.<br /><br />As a future teacher, I would highly recommend this as a companion piece, if not a replacement, to Huckleberry Finn due to this book's easier readability. If not for the whole class, it would be a good replacement for English learners or students with special needs.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_618598062" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618598062" />
    <a title="Ninth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16228867-ninth"><img alt="Ninth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406345299p2/16228867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618598062?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ninth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ninth " href="/user/show/16228867-ninth">Ninth </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618598062" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7427768941166190860"><b>5 stars. <i>THWACK!</i></b><br/><br/>I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br/><br/>Jebel Rum is a thin kid. Even if he eats like me, he still remains thin and small and weak.<br/><br/>His father, Rashed Rum, is the EXECUTIONER! And that's not a fact to sneer at. Executioners are only second to the Ruler of the Abu Aineh.<br/><br/>Rashed is the best Executioner they ever had ir ever would have. Only one chop and heads roll.   <span id="freeText7427768941166190860" style="display:none"><b>5 stars. <i>THWACK!</i></b><br /><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br /><br />Jebel Rum is a thin kid. Even if he eats like me, he still remains thin and small and weak.<br /><br />His father, Rashed Rum, is the EXECUTIONER! And that's not a fact to sneer at. Executioners are only second to the Ruler of the Abu Aineh.<br /><br />Rashed is the best Executioner they ever had ir ever would have. Only one chop and heads roll. In Abu Aineh, Every crime, whether it was murder of a king or stealing a piece of moldy rotten bread, was punished in one way and one way only- EXECUTION.<br /><br /><b>Thwack!<br />"Next!"</b><br /><br />So..Rashed had three sons, J'An, J'Al and Jebel. Rashed was old, so he needed a succesor. The successor was to be decided by a contest and people knew that the 2 Muscular J'An or J'Al would win. Rashed spoke...he said that he would feel AWESOME if his successor was J'An or J'Al... He did not even mention Jebel.<br /><br />THAT WAS A DISGRACE. Jebel felt horrible. He could not live in shame. He had to show them that he could do stuff. But how?<br /><br />By a girl named Bastina, the servant of BOOT-i-Ful Debbat Alg, he indirectly got an idea. He could quest north to the mountains to petition Sabbah Eid, The God of fire, who granys invincibility to those who are successful. But a slave must be sacrificed. Who?<br /><br />Tel Hesani, an Um Keshabah, agrees. In return he asks his wife and children be set free. <br /><br />AGREED. SIGNED. SEALED.<br /><br />So they journey. They could reach their destination easily by waters. But that was the challenge of the quest, they must not use waterways.<br /><br />Land is filled with different kind of people- the Snake worshippers from Abu Nekhele to the Deadly Warriors of Abu Siq.<br /><br />The story is in a third person narrative. So it lets us know the feelings of both the quester and his slave. <br /><br />Jebel, is a spolit son of A-B, bloody brat. He thinks of slaves as shit. Arrogant beyond measure. Hates all who differs from his belief of gods. Despices all who take kindly to slaves. All in all, he is thick headed because of his royal family.<br /><br />Tel Hesani, a wise man, A slave yet so brave, protects Jebel like a father, tries to talk sense into him and stuff. Above all, he is ready to sacrifice himself for his family.<br /><br />One thing is for sure, Darren Shan surely crafted the protagonist in such a way that everyone must ABSOLUTELY HATE HIM. I did the same, I'd have sent him for execution straight away. He treats Tel Hesani like Scum. But Tel Hesani's faith doesn't waver.<br /><br />Along the travel they meet all kind of deadly creatures. Tel expertly helps Jebel even though Jebel is not thankful. They get acquainted with two traders called Master Bush and Blair, who bring them fortune and its antonym.<br /><br />They meet deadly warriors, wonderful artista, Bat-lovers <br /><br />aaaand<br /><br />even CANNIBALS.<br /><br />I can say no more...You must read it. This is a tale on life. How people regard others and how they actually should. The transformation of a spoiler brat into a noble man, how he changed. Why he changed. What made him change.<br /><br /><br />BRILLIANT!<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText12850358816461005411" style="display:none">No other book has been sitting on my shelves unread for so long as this one. But I had no idea what to expect of this story, this is an author-buy for me. <br /><br />It turns out, I really like the idea of this story. <div id="review_1776689266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1776689266" />
    <a title="Lör K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59592712-l-r-k"><img alt="Lör K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549951102p2/59592712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776689266?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lör K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lör K." href="/user/show/59592712-l-r-k">Lör K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15813455-the-thin-executioner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=horror-recommendations">horror-recommendations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=would-read-again">would-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59592712-l-r-k?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776689266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17928341746218363307">From young adult horror author Darren Shan, comes the wonderfully dark and tense story, <i>The Thing Executioner</i>.<br/><br/>Meet Jebel, the executioner's son. He's scrawny, has barely any strength, and is considered a mockery. A weak son of an executioner? Hard to believe. But then, a quest arises, that allows Jebel the possibility to become the man he's always wanted to be.<br/><br/>When this first came out, I was really excited to read it. The moment my library got a copy, I got it out before anyone else could. Unfor</span>
  <span id="freeText17928341746218363307" style="display:none">From young adult horror author Darren Shan, comes the wonderfully dark and tense story, <i>The Thing Executioner</i>.<br /><br />Meet Jebel, the executioner's son. He's scrawny, has barely any strength, and is considered a mockery. A weak son of an executioner? Hard to believe. But then, a quest arises, that allows Jebel the possibility to become the man he's always wanted to be.<br /><br />When this first came out, I was really excited to read it. The moment my library got a copy, I got it out before anyone else could. Unfortunately, I never had the time to read it because I was going through a lot of tests at school, and my whole time was dedicated to revising. Heartbroken, I took it back to the library, putting myself immediately on the reserve list - it would have been months before I even got the chance to read it. Much to my surprise, my sister got me it for my birthday the month after, and I immediately started reading it. I wasn't letting it get away again!<br /><br />What I found within these pages was a beautifully created magical land with such diverse and developed characters that I felt my heart be stolen just two chapters in. Each page just creates even more beauty that it hurt my soul, I wanted nothing more to be taken into this book and never be allowed to leave. I didn't want to finish this. It was stunning.<br /><br />Shan's writing, just like with every other book he's written, was enrapturing. The words flowed so easily and it was so easy to just turn the page and be lost in the world he has created. The characters are beautifully diverse and well written, and there is so much development throughout the story that all the characters felt beautifully fleshed out. I wanted Jebel to be my best friend, he was so stunningly written. The moral behind the whole story really took me by surprise, (and in all honesty, when it happened, I felt a little deflated - but it picks up so quickly) and I think it was a beautiful moral behind the story of it all.<br /><br />This is a stand alone book, but I cannot scream about how much I would <b>love</b> for Shan to revisit this and create another book. It was simply stunning and it seems like such a shame to write only one book about such a magical land.<br /><br />This is a definite recommendation from me, and I would kill to be able to reread this book at some point. I just need more of it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17928341746218363307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120094392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120094392" />
    <a title="Ace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3404142-ace"><img alt="Ace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1273887924p2/3404142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120094392?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ace" href="/user/show/3404142-ace">Ace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316129107" href="/book/show/8658726-the-thin-executioner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120094392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7294732581059519444">Jebel is one of the sons of the executioner in their town (I forgot the name), a thin and accused as weak unlike his brothers. Time has come for his father to retire from being an executioner, so he endorse his two sons excluding Jebel to join a competition to become the next executioner.Because of his pride, Jebel think of joining the competition, but he knows it himself that he can't win the game. <br/><br/>There is only one way for him to gain the strength he needs to win the competition, Jebel need to</span>
  <span id="freeText7294732581059519444" style="display:none">Jebel is one of the sons of the executioner in their town (I forgot the name), a thin and accused as weak unlike his brothers. Time has come for his father to retire from being an executioner, so he endorse his two sons excluding Jebel to join a competition to become the next executioner.Because of his pride, Jebel think of joining the competition, but he knows it himself that he can't win the game. <br /><br />There is only one way for him to gain the strength he needs to win the competition, Jebel need to do a quest, he need to go in a certain mountain to seek for the god. For him to be granted a quest, he must find a slave who he can offer to the God of that mountain and ask for the invincibility he needs to win the competition. He didn't fail on finding a slave for his quest and for that, he was granted a quest... This is where the story began...<br /><br />The book tackles about the equality of the people living in that place, the relationship of a slave and the master. Shan also touched the most controversial topic, religion, though he wrote it in a fictitious and gruesome way (One of the scenes in the book is really disgusting that made me want to vomit). He is lucid on the message he wanted to tell his readers.<br /><br />And in the end, Shan showed that nobody is perfect whether you're in a high or in the lowest society, and everybody can be a tool for a change, it is not based on the status you have in your life.<br /><br />Shan is really a good story teller. He can make you move and can keep you amazed all throughout his novel, this is what I felt while reading his Cirque Du Freak and The Thin Executioner. And because of this, I will certainly say that I am a fan of him. <br /><br />And by the way, the ending? Did I say "The Ending"? Oh! The ENDING!<br /><br /><i>*** The names of the characters and places are weird, so I really can't remember the names except for the protagonist, Jebel... </i><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7294732581059519444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_85438236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85438236" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/170420-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228387079p2/170420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85438236?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/170420-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/170420-laura?shelf=mt-bookpile-2010">mt-bookpile-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/170420-laura?shelf=old-reads">old-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer85438236&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85438236" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2876885449932392265">This is <i>not</i> the book to read if you're looking for another Darren Shan horror/gorefest: it is very unlike the <i>Cirque du Freak</i> and <i>Demonata</i> series. It <i>is</i> the book to read if you're looking for an adventure/trek story set in a different world than ours.<br/><br/>Jebel is a third son, thin and unlike his brothers, not to mention his father, the Chief Executioner in a city that prizes strength and skill. His honor at stake after his father fails to mention him as a potential successor, Jebel decides to go on </span>
  <span id="freeText2876885449932392265" style="display:none">This is <i>not</i> the book to read if you're looking for another Darren Shan horror/gorefest: it is very unlike the <i>Cirque du Freak</i> and <i>Demonata</i> series. It <i>is</i> the book to read if you're looking for an adventure/trek story set in a different world than ours.<br /><br />Jebel is a third son, thin and unlike his brothers, not to mention his father, the Chief Executioner in a city that prizes strength and skill. His honor at stake after his father fails to mention him as a potential successor, Jebel decides to go on a quest to find invincibility. With his newly purchased slave, Tel Hesani, at his side, he sets off.<br /><br />This world feels vaguely Middle Eastern, and vaguely Middle Ages. There's no technology, much hand-to-mouth existence, slavery and religious ritual in a desert setting. One village has a definite Petra quality (never a bad thing). While on this quest, Jebel's attitudes and beliefs slowly - and I do mean slowly - change. When he starts, he's among the elite in his society yet by the end he's been a slave, starved and suffered many physical privations. One could argue that his mere survival is proof of his invincibility!<br /><br />His return to Wadi fails to garner him his father's approval, and the lessons learned while on his quest ultimately have a great impact on this culture he left. I'm not sure I totally buy his "conversion", in part because we only get glimpses of it during the quest itself. However, by the end I felt that it was the only course for this character to have taken.<br /><br />ARC provided by publisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2876885449932392265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5475609838516659288" style="display:none">This is a book that really drawing me in! Darren Shann never fail to attract my attention of reading his books. I like his Cirque Du Freak books and this one is also is a very good premise. It starts with an awful beginning as the head rolling and also the sound of how the head cut from the neck of the prisoners. I thought, "I'm not good with with this dreadful reading stuff". Turn out, it is not so bad at all.<br /><br />Thin executioner is actually introducing us a very thin young man who is on a quest with his slave to a far away on highest mountain to harbor a fierce God to give him a superhuman strength so that he could prove to everyone back ta home that he's also worthy man to be honored like his two brothers. However, the quest with his slave open his eyes about the outside world since he's been thought that his tribe is very respectable tribe compared to others. His character is so arrogant, proud, selfish, and he likes to snort. While he's slave/companion is very humble, obedient, sometime very optimistic for a slave. He's also very patient with Jebel's grunts and sulking. Every characters are well described and yes, they are quite interesting. Shann imaginations in his writing is very impressive.<br /><br />The book has a fast pace, likely a page turner, imaginative, interesting, alluring your interest and imagination. It may sound quite disturbing whenever Jebel remembers how the executions stuff, heads rolling and everything but I ensure you that the book has so much to give. The story itself is very adventurous, engaging and very consistent excitements. Although they have quite a lot of<br />adventures in a very short period like in 2 or 3 chapters, every adventures ends with a good closure, very well put and no cliff hanger.<br /><br />It maybe sounds a bit weird, but I really enjoyed reading the book, very much. And I should tell you this, I was quite frustrated with the ending but it was satisfying once you know why</span>

  <span id="freeText7878321835161094583" style="display:none">I love Darren Shan books, I just don't read enough of them. <div id="review_2091420025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091420025" />
    <a title="Callum Biggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32932693-callum-biggs"><img alt="Callum Biggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593444354p2/32932693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091420025?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Callum Biggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Callum Biggs" href="/user/show/32932693-callum-biggs">Callum Biggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091420025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8584550918249447130">For my first Darren Shan book, my experience was one mixed with highs and lows. Initially the story took a while to get me interested as it lacks detail and any meaningful relationships between the characters from the offset.<br/><br/>As Jebel Rum's journey got going I was intrigued to see where it would go as there was lots of room for creativity along the way. The many populations of people scattered across their path made for an interesting read as they all held differing customs and beliefs which help</span>
  <span id="freeText8584550918249447130" style="display:none">For my first Darren Shan book, my experience was one mixed with highs and lows. Initially the story took a while to get me interested as it lacks detail and any meaningful relationships between the characters from the offset.<br /><br />As Jebel Rum's journey got going I was intrigued to see where it would go as there was lots of room for creativity along the way. The many populations of people scattered across their path made for an interesting read as they all held differing customs and beliefs which helped to add some depth to the land the characters were in.<br /><br />However with every village they passed it became a little predictable with near scares and lack of intelligence of the village people to allow strangers in which would about their downfall.<br /><br />The relationship between the two questers grew from complete strangers to close companions. They learned from each other greatly and I enjoyed to see their development throughout. In the end everything fell together nicely and I particularly liked how the morals of the villagers in terms of killing were questioned by Jebel due to his experiences he had gained along his quest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8584550918249447130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1922015042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922015042" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58731934-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471919928p2/58731934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922015042?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/58731934-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1922015042&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922015042" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2807823930519039747">This book by Darren Shan called The Thin Executioner was an excellent book. It's about the journey of a runt of a boy who is the son of the best executioner in the lands, Rashed Rum, and a slave named Tel Hesani. The boy, who's named Jebel Rum, wants redemption because he is so small and thin. He is considered a disgrace in is family. He has two older brother that are exactly like his father. He wants redemption by becoming the new executioner, which is achievable soon because his father is beco</span>
  <span id="freeText2807823930519039747" style="display:none">This book by Darren Shan called The Thin Executioner was an excellent book. It's about the journey of a runt of a boy who is the son of the best executioner in the lands, Rashed Rum, and a slave named Tel Hesani. The boy, who's named Jebel Rum, wants redemption because he is so small and thin. He is considered a disgrace in is family. He has two older brother that are exactly like his father. He wants redemption by becoming the new executioner, which is achievable soon because his father is becoming old. He travels through the lands with his slave in search of Sabbah Eid, a god that could grant him invincibility. Jebel and his slave get separated because of some traitors and liars, but they manage to find the god. Before they found him, Tel Hesani becomes injured from a fight and soon dies, but that was good because the god needed a sacrifice anyways. In the end, Jebel returns home and wins the competition to become the new executioner. The next day, Jebel needed to kill a criminal, but he didn't have the heart, so he sacrificed himself. Fortunately, going on the quest made him invincible so he lived and the criminal was saved. he did this with every single criminal that came to the block. Soon, his land became overrun with thieves. He ended becoming tall and big, but he remained thin.<br /><br />I rated this book 5 stars because of all the excitement and the description of the characters. There were also some moments in the book when the heroes were in danger, like being hung, but they managed escape. The downside on this book is that I feel that the author hurried the ending up because he wanted to get it over with. This book also must have a second book to it because the story doesn't seem to be complete yet. What I mean is that this book needs something to top it off. Like in the part where the thieves were everywhere, there were no details on how to stop them. Overall, this book was one of the very best I've ever read. I recommend this book to anybody that enjoys a fantasy book that also has the ability to pass some time. These types of books are, in fact, very rare to find.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2807823930519039747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_378970515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xustine Yee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xustine Yee" href="/user/show/2773385-xustine-yee">Xustine Yee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2773385-xustine-yee?shelf=summer-reading-2012-2013">summer-reading-2012-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2773385-xustine-yee?shelf=advisory-2012-2013">advisory-2012-2013</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer378970515&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378970515" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699911172373083904">The Thin Executioner was a decent book. I'd give it 3.5 stars. As a Darren Shan fanatic, i had high expectations for this book. i expected a twisted, complicated plot with sinister details and gruesome imagery that would make Steven Spielberg shiver. However, it wasn't that fulfilling at all. <br/><br/>Pro's:<br/>1. the huge array of characters that the two protagonists meets. They were all interesting and had different personalities (some were freaking cannibals, some were people who hurt themselves to repent</span>
  <span id="freeText3699911172373083904" style="display:none">The Thin Executioner was a decent book. I'd give it 3.5 stars. As a Darren Shan fanatic, i had high expectations for this book. i expected a twisted, complicated plot with sinister details and gruesome imagery that would make Steven Spielberg shiver. However, it wasn't that fulfilling at all. <br /><br />Pro's:<br />1. the huge array of characters that the two protagonists meets. They were all interesting and had different personalities (some were freaking cannibals, some were people who hurt themselves to repent their sins, some worship dead heads, etc.)<br />2. The writing style that Shan used. He added in just the right amount of imagery details to make me able to imagine it, but not make me bored. <br />3. The plot<br /><br />Con's:<br />1. The plot, although interesting, was very unoriginal and corny. I was able to see right through it and predict the ending. a boy is different from his family, he sets out with a "slave" as sacrifice to a god so he can become strong, the slave protects him through the journey, boy starts to become attached to slave, boy doesn't want to sacrifice slave when time comes, etc. Yeah, that kind of predictable. <br />2. THE NAMES IN THE BOOK OF THE TRIBES, PEOPLE, OBJECTS, GODS, and PLACES. oh my god. i wish there was a reference in the back or something because it drove me mad. the names seemed like they were created by someone who sneezed and banged his hand on the keyboard. There were just too many places with names that sounded too similar that i couldn't take it.<br />3. wasn't gruesome enough. i wanted HORROR. but, oh well. it was still a good read :)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260578333?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/5212582-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5212582-lee?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260578333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15661236008315285374">I wouldn't have laid eyes on any of Darren Shan's works if it wasn't for my sister, who was the one who borrowed it for me. Initially, I was hesitant to read the book since I haven't heard of the author. Another reason why I was skeptical is because Jebel Rum wasn't exactly a protagonist that interested me to the very least. Unless of course he happened to be ran over by a tractor and bitten by twenty thousand eight hundred poisonous snakes. Jebel was arrogant, conceited and to put it bluntly, e</span>
  <span id="freeText15661236008315285374" style="display:none">I wouldn't have laid eyes on any of Darren Shan's works if it wasn't for my sister, who was the one who borrowed it for me. Initially, I was hesitant to read the book since I haven't heard of the author. Another reason why I was skeptical is because Jebel Rum wasn't exactly a protagonist that interested me to the very least. Unless of course he happened to be ran over by a tractor and bitten by twenty thousand eight hundred poisonous snakes. Jebel was arrogant, conceited and to put it bluntly, exasperating. Of course, the way he was brought up to believe could also be factored in to how he sees lives.<br /><br />Nevertheless, I read on because I was excited to see what would happen to our egotistical hero. All the adventures he was going through, from being a grave robber to his casual brush with a god of death, were gripping, mesmerizing and just attention-catching. There were also scenes wherein the gore was expected but it still made your stomach turn. All in all, it's a good book that will take you on an adventure beyond your wildest dreams.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15661236008315285374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shahrun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6192290-shahrun"><img alt="Shahrun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465419853p2/6192290.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1803259194&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803259194" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5672702863508796536">Darren Shan is a Master Storyteller! This book tells the story of Jebel Rum. He is the runt of the litter and feels it. When his father publicly overlooks him, as a possible candidate to replace him as Town Executioner (a very highly prized and esteemed job), he rashly decides the only path for redemption is to go on a Quest. We then set off with this arrogant, selfish & unworldly boy and his newly acquired slave Tel Hesani on the most dangerous and brutal journey. You've got to read it to belie</span>
  <span id="freeText5672702863508796536" style="display:none">Darren Shan is a Master Storyteller! This book tells the story of Jebel Rum. He is the runt of the litter and feels it. When his father publicly overlooks him, as a possible candidate to replace him as Town Executioner (a very highly prized and esteemed job), he rashly decides the only path for redemption is to go on a Quest. We then set off with this arrogant, selfish &amp; unworldly boy and his newly acquired slave Tel Hesani on the most dangerous and brutal journey. You've got to read it to believe what happened to them! I loved the fact that the journey slowly changes Jebel for the better. He then chooses to stick by his new found knowledge and understanding. Even when that pretty much makes him a social outcast. This book maybe set in a different time and different place, but Darren Shan has somehow managed to tell us what is wrong with this world - today! He addresses War, Conquesting, Slavery, Religion, The Death Penalty/Penal system... Aside from the amazing story, it has given me much to thing about regarding society in general. Wow!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5672702863508796536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Aldana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Aldana" href="/user/show/21498912-allison-aldana">Allison Aldana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2230036820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14307437255392698567">Okay so.....<br/>I liked the premise of the book. And the beginning of Jebel's journey was interesting. It kinda lagged in the middle when Shan really rubbed it into your face that Jebel was suffering. It was too much telling and not really enough showing.<br/>Once Jebel reunited with Tel Hasani it picked back up again. <br/>The last few pages were a little cheesy but I reminded myself that this book seems to be aimed at a younger end of YA so I can't expect it to not be heavy handed.<br/><br/>I had put this book down f</span>
  <span id="freeText14307437255392698567" style="display:none">Okay so.....<br />I liked the premise of the book. And the beginning of Jebel's journey was interesting. It kinda lagged in the middle when Shan really rubbed it into your face that Jebel was suffering. It was too much telling and not really enough showing.<br />Once Jebel reunited with Tel Hasani it picked back up again. <br />The last few pages were a little cheesy but I reminded myself that this book seems to be aimed at a younger end of YA so I can't expect it to not be heavy handed.<br /><br />I had put this book down for a long while before finishing it and I think the general enthusiasm just wasn't there anymore. It really put a damper on how I feel about the book. I think I would have liked it a lot more if I had read it all at once. The characters didn't really resonate with me in any way.<br /><br />I like... the idea of the book. I think I've just been reading and planning on reading a whole bunch of hardcore epic fantasy that this fell a little flat for me.<br /><br />Don't take this review too seriously, I guess. (not that anyone is reading this, lets be honest here)</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1491640510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6940817134049403262">I read this book in one long sitting, on a train.<br/><br/>This one is great. I've read about eighteen of Shan's work, and I could see resemblance and difference aplenty. There was little over the top salughter such as in the demonata, more positivity than in the Darren shan series, but you still got that "Oh" moment of someone being horrible. I simply cannot recommend this book enough.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('820EeO4UAsETBA2nh2q7CzAGSO6z4VYrJ1qa7ZRaM4WU9Lw1+9sQVmPQjDqGT3sM176Pj+mAGMSq3Zgo4lgmlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

To escape the gods\' revenge, Prometheus travels through time to a murky metropolis called Eden City.<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17048607833504301583\" style=\"display:none\">International best-selling author Terry Deary reinvents the myth of Prometheus, the Titan who stole fire from the gods and gave it to the human race. To escape the gods\' revenge, Prometheus travels through time to a murky metropolis called Eden City. There he befriends a motley assortment of comic characters and learns what humans have done with his gift of fire. Enter our narrator: the resourceful and plucky 12 year old Nell.   <span id="freeText5369708916251142467" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
